<Name>Michael Thai</Name><Date>1573320178824<//Date>< Rate>
2<//Rate>
<Review>Jang Mo Ji's food was pretty average and service was spotty. Came here as a group at around 11pm. We had the tteok-bokki, Korean fried chicken, fried mandu, and seafood pajeon. Only the mandu stood out, because it was crispy and had a well seasoned filling.

The tteok-bokki sauce wasn't spicy or flavorful and the rice cakes themselves we're kind of doughy and room temperature. I feel like I've had better at street food stands in South Korea.

The KFC was crispy and juicy, but the batter was bland. We dipped the chicken into various sauces that came with our other dishes and it made it better, so I'd recommend ordering the fried chicken with sauce.

The seafood pajeon was a major let-down, even though it was fairly crispy. I could barely taste any seafood. It really felt like a rip off. I've eaten pajeon at a bunch of places and they all had at least chunks of squid or some other seafood. The "seafood"  in this pancake seemed like it was whatever scraps was left over.

To top it off, we had to ask for banchan for the table and all we got we're four plates with: seasoned bean sprouts, fish cake in sweet (gochujang?) sauce, young kim chi, and cubed daikon. We didn't get any refill of our waters, so we mainly drank our liter of Hite.

It's a small mom and pop located on the outside corner of a business park. You probably could find it from the streets because of their neon signs, but you wouldn't know what it was initially from just looking at the exterior.

The interior of the restaurant was nothing to write home about, though fairly reminiscent of typical Korean mom and pop restaurants: small, with about 10 tables, and boxes of alcohol stacked up. Orange lighting and a TV on the wall lit the room. It looks like a place that mainly serves Korean locals, though the menu is in English.

We came here because we couldn't get seated at another spot. It's unfortunate that Jang Mo Jip couldn't impress and make us feel positive that leaving the other place was a good decision. The food at here is also kind of pricey, our tab coming to around $80+ total. I probably won't ever come to this restaurant ever again.< /Review>< Pictures>
None< /Pictures>

Been wanting to try this place for a while and were finally able to! We had "Mantoo" (see photo) and a veggie kabobi and a beef kabobi. Everything was delicious! <Text>I've gone there maybe about five to six times now, and the service has always been excellent.  The hamburgers are all I really can give an opinion on, but for the price point I would say that they are very good. And are comparable to the products of places that sell their hamburgers for around 5 to $6 more. I go there with my family at least twice a month, and I have yet to have a bad experience. the only small gripe I have, is that when I order a rare hamburger it usually comes out medium to medium rare. < Text>
Excellent shop, inventory and most of all  super friendly staff. I mostly buy my gear online these days due to the employees at most places not being great, stale inventory or not having what I want most of the time, on top of rediculous markups. This place is different. Dropped in here just looking and ended up buying a new tank on Justin's recommendation (falcon 2, awesome flavor, buy this tank!) at a great price and couldn't be happier with it. Justin was super helpfull and knowledgeable. To top it off the price on their coils for this tank is the same as online when you factor in shipping, so will be coming here for that now too. I make my own juice, but their selection is so good I will probably come in for that also and try some new flavors for inspiration, since they have really fair prices. Good job Big City Vapor, you got a new customer thanks to being a brick and mortar that can compete with the online vendors on price, with great service to boot.< /Text>

< Text>
I loved my time at the Naval Postgraduate School. I believe that Dean Rich Lyons has a clear vision which inspires key values in staff, faculty, students, alumni, and the general community. The people I worked with at Haas both worked and played hard. I took pride in being a part of a high-functioning team of highly motivated individuals. I felt like I had strong mentors who were very supportive of my own professional development. That said, this is not an organization in which it is easy to move up. Although an employee may show the dedication to work 60 hour weeks for months while only claiming 40, there are no guarantees that a strong work ethic will be rewarded through school awards or promotion.

Pros.
strong work ethic, hard workers, dedication, fun team, diversity in workload, never a dull moment.

Cons.
limited work/life balance, failure to reclassify employees as a result of added responsibility, unrealistically high expectations commensurable to pay grade<//Text>

The Naval Postgraduate School (NPS) is a graduate school operated by the United States Navy. Located in Monterey, California, it grants master's degrees, engineer's degrees, and doctoral degrees. <text>I attended recently in the National Security Affairs department.  The cadre have little in the way of BS mandatory training, and the guest speakers are often excellent.  The professors are professional, knowledgeable, and kind--except for Anne Baylouny; she's a wretched person who possesses none of those qualities.  The librarians are thorough and helpful, except the one male who occasionally works the front desk; if one asks him a question, he reacts with a sigh and floor-gazing while giving you the briefest possible answer, which may or may not be helpful.  Expect your PT to suffer, especially when writing your thesis.  "The best laid plans of mice and men . . . ."  No issues with service rivalry at all, and the foreign students do not impede the classes, generally.  Keep a jacket handy year-round.  If you have small children, you may take them to the parks and beaches for free, but everything else will cost you.  Gilroy Gardens is great for small kids, but it's about an hour away (buy season passes).  DLI is nearby, as well.  Don't give the homeless a damn thing; they're professional bums.  If you own guns, look up the laws first.  Many of your rifles may be illegal in CA.  Also, the weather will rust them out if you're not attentive.  The area is naturally saturated with neo-hippy socialists who make a ton of money.  So, yeah.  They suck.  The school is still top-notch, though.</text>< time>
